### Post by mahound2 on 2014-06-02
Hi,

I have a laptop that its model is Hp Pavilion DV6-2300. it had Windows 7 and I installed ubuntu 13 on it. The system worked find for osme years. but yesterday, the laptop powered off some times because of some reasons. now when I turn it up, it shows me a error message such as below:

error: no such partition

grub rescue>

some solutions I found such as follow:

fdisk -l

mkdir /mnt/temp

mount -t ext3 -o dev /dev/sda3 /mnt/temp

output of last commond:

ount: wrong fs type, bad option, bad superblock on /dev/sda3,
       missing codepage or helper program, or other error
       In some cases useful info is found in syslog - try
       dmesg | tail  or so
and output of dmesg command

[ 7781.700726] attempt to access beyond end of device
[ 7781.700734] sda3: rw=0, want=4, limit=2
[ 7781.700741] EXT3-fs (sda3): error: unable to read superblock

does it mean a superblock has been damaged??
how can I repair it??

thanks

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-06-02
First try fsck.

 #From liveDVD/Flash so everything is unmounted,swap off if necessary, change example shown with partition sdb1 to your partition(s)
#e2fsck is used to check the ext2/ext3/ext4 family of file systems. -p trys fixes where response not required
sudo e2fsck -C0 -p -f -v /dev/sdb1
#if errors: -y auto answers yes for fixes needing response, also see man e2fsck
sudo e2fsck -f -y -v /dev/sdb1

If not, then more advanced change examples to your partition(s):

 [http://linuxexpresso.wordpress.com/2010/03/31/repair-a-broken-ext4-superblock-in-ubuntu/](http://linuxexpresso.wordpress.com/2010/03/31/repair-a-broken-ext4-superblock-in-ubuntu/)
Remove first inode to use alternative superblock:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1682038](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1682038)
Using alternative superblock to check ext3
[http://planet.admon.org/using-alternative-superblock-to-check-ext3/](http://planet.admon.org/using-alternative-superblock-to-check-ext3/)
List backup superblocks:
sudo dumpe2fs /dev/sda5 | grep -i backup
then use backup superblock, 32768 just an example, try several
sudo fsck -b 32768 /dev/sda5
One user could not get partition unmounted (may have needed swapoff), but used another live distro

---

### Post by Bashing-om on 2014-06-02
mahound2; Hi ! My Welcome to the forum.

Could be a minor file system glitch, and as major as hard drive failure - they do not last forever - or perhaps the boot code has become corrupted.

Boot up the liveDVD, and from "disk utility" run the full SMART test.

If that passes then we can look at running a file system check for the ubuntu install:
Post back - Between code tags, Please - the outputs of terminal commands:
```

sudo fdisk -lu
sudo parted -l

```
so we know what we are working with and we can then provide the correct command(s) to run the file system checks.
code tag tutorial:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2171721&p=12776168#post12776168](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2171721&p=12776168#post12776168)


When SMART is good, file system verified then we look at the boot code.

[INDENT][INDENT]in the process of 
[INDENT][INDENT][INDENT]elimination
[/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT]

### Post by oldfred on 2014-06-02
Your extended partition seems to have a lot of unused space that probably was the Linux partition. You should be able to use testdisk to restore it.

 3 430GB 486GB 56.2GB extended lba
5 482GB 486GB 3747MB logical linux-swap(v1)

      
 Testdisk Instructions
[http://www.cgsecurity.org/wiki/TestDisk_Step_By_Step](http://www.cgsecurity.org/wiki/TestDisk_Step_By_Step)
[http://www.cgsecurity.org/wiki/Menu_Analyse](http://www.cgsecurity.org/wiki/Menu_Analyse)

Windows rewrote partition table without the Linux partition.

```

sudo apt-get install testdisk

```

### Post by Bashing-om on 2014-06-04
mahound2; Hey !

Looks good, let's (RE-)install ubuntus's boot manager:
Must be done from the liveDVD/USB so;
Boot up the liveDVD to a terminal:
```

sudo mount /dev/sda1 /mnt
sudo grub-install --boot-directory=/mnt/ /dev/sda
sudo umount /mnt

```

Reboot and reset in bios to boot the 1st hard drive;
I expect at this time will boot up ubuntu.
Now from the install -> terminal:
```

sudo grub-install --recheck /dev/sda
sudo update-grub

```

Reboot once more.

[INDENT][INDENT]Tell us now
[INDENT][INDENT][INDENT][INDENT]all is fine good and dandy
[/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT]

### Post by oldfred on 2014-06-04
It looks like you recovered the Linux partition, but did not include the NTFS partitions at the beginning of the drive.
And it reordered the partitions, so the Linux partitions that were in the extended partition are now primary partitions even though still located at the end of the drive. 
It shows lots of space, now before sda1.

You need to include all you partitions in recovery in testdisk and make sure the Linux partition is logical not primary. That may force you to update grub again as partition changes/deletions may change UUID and then you need updates. 

From your early post:
```
Device Boot      Start         End      Blocks   Id  System
/dev/sda1   *        2048      409599      203776    7  HPFS/NTFS
Partition 1 does not end on cylinder boundary.
/dev/sda2          409600   839270399   419430400    7  HPFS/NTFS
Partition 2 does not end on cylinder boundary.
/dev/sda3       839272446   948991999    54859777    f  W95 Ext'd (LBA)
Partition 3 does not end on cylinder boundary.
/dev/sda4       948992000   976560127    13784064    7  HPFS/NTFS
/dev/sda5       941674496   948991999     3658752   82  Linux swap / Solaris
```

And what you now show:
```
Device Boot      Start         End      Blocks   Id  System
/dev/sda1   *   839272448   941674495    51201024   83  Linux
/dev/sda2       948992000   976560127    13784064    7  HPFS/NTFS
/dev/sda3       976560128   976773119      106496    c  W95 FAT32 (LBA)
```

Your sda1 is where your missing Linux partition was in the extended partition sda3. Your sda2 used to be sda4. Swap was lost a bit of unused space at end of drive become a FAT32 partition. 
But the sectors where original sda1 & ssda2 were is not shown and they are now the missing partitions.
Your Linux probably was sda5 and swap was sda6 before all the changes started.
